The Market Value of an Umm Walad: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on market value of umm walad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the market value of an umm walad, explain the proofs from Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) in guarantee cases.

Core Idea
An umm walad has no market value for Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn assign her one-third a regular slave's value.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether an umm walad (a slave-girl who has borne her master's child) has a market value (taqawwum). Imam Abu Hanifa holds that she has no value because she is not saleable, while the two Sahibayn argue that she does have value because she can be benefited from. The disagreement rests on conflicting hadith interpretations. Understanding this dispute clarifies the school's method of resolving textual conflicts and the role of istihsan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions and the hukm level
Read the opening: 'وما لأم ولد تقوم'. Note that Abu Hanifa says لا قيمة (no value), while the Sahibayn say لها قيمة (she has value). This is a dispute over property status (hukm wad'i), not a taklifi ruling.
The term تقوم refers to having a market value for compensation purposes.
2
Examine Abu Hanifa's dalil
Abu Hanifa cites the hadith of 'Ali: 'أعتقها ولدها' (her child frees her), implying immediate freedom which removes value. The text notes that this hadith is reported by Ibn Majah and al-Daraqutni.
This hadith has zanni thubut and dalala, but Abu Hanifa views it as decisive for negating value.
3
Analyse the Sahibayn's reasoning and counter-dalil
The Sahibayn argue that the umm walad is owned and can be benefited from (intercourse, hire, use), so she should have value like a mudabbir. They support this with another hadith: 'أيما أمة ولدت سيدها فهي معتقة عن دبر منه' (reported by Ahmad), which makes freedom only after the master's death, preserving value during life.
The Sahibayn's value is set at ثلث قيمة القن (one-third the value of a regular slave).
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
The practical difference arises in guarantee cases: if someone seizes or frees another's umm walad, Abu Hanifa says no liability (since she has no value), while the Sahibayn say liability for half her value. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the school is Abu Hanifa's view.
The text states 'فلا يضمن' – 'so he does not guarantee' – indicating the mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما لأم ولد تقوم هذا نصف بيت من الرجز أخذه الشيخ عن "المنظومة" للنسفي، أي ليس لها قيمة عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا لها قيمة؛ لأنه ينتفع بها وطئاً وإجارة واستخداماً وهي مملوكة محرزة فتكون مقومة كالمدبر، ولهذا لو قال: كل مملوك لي حر تدخل أم الولد فيه واستباحة الوطء دليل الملك، وقيمتها ثلث قيمة القن وبه قالت الثلاثة، وله قوله علي: "أعتقها ولدها"، رواه ابن ماجة والدار قطني وقضيته الحرية زوال التقوم، لكنه تقاعد عن إفادة الحرية لعارض، وهو قوله عليه: "أيما أمة ولدت سيدها فهي معتقة عن دبر منه" أو قال: "من بعده"، رواه أحمد ولا معارض له في زوال التقوم فثبت ما ذكرنا. [رمز الحقائق: ٣٢٩/١] فلا يضمن بيان لثمرة الخلاف بين الإمام وصاحبيه. (محشي)
And 'what is for umm walad has value?' This is half a verse of rajaz that the shaykh took from al-Nasafi's Manzuma. That is, she has no value according to Abu Hanifa. And they (the two Sahibayn) said she has value, because one benefits from her by intercourse, hire, and use, and she is owned and guarded, so she has value like a mudabbir. For this reason, if he said: 'Every slave I own is free,' the umm walad enters, and the permissibility of intercourse is evidence of ownership. Her value is one-third of the value of a regular slave, and the three (imams) said this. And he (Abu Hanifa) adduces the saying of 'Ali: 'Her child frees her' (reported by Ibn Majah and al-Daraqutni), and its import is that freedom removes value. But this (hadith) fails to confer freedom due to an obstruction, which is his saying: 'Any slave-girl who bears a child to her master is free after his death' (reported by Ahmad), and there is no contradiction in the removal of value, so what we mentioned is established. [Reference: Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1/329] So he does not guarantee – a statement of the result of the difference between the Imam and his two companions.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage addresses a fundamental dispute: does an umm walad (a slave-girl who has borne her master's child) have a market value (qīma)? Imam Abu Hanifa holds that she has no value because she is not saleable and her freedom upon the master's death overrides any monetary consideration. She is considered like a free person in terms of value. The two Sahibayn, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, argue that she does have value because she can be benefited from through intercourse, hiring, and use, and she is owned property, albeit restricted in sale. They liken her to a mudabbir (who also is not sold but has value). The text presents a proof from a saying of 'Ali: 'Her child frees her,' which Abu Hanifa interprets as meaning she becomes free and therefore loses value. The Sahibayn counter with a hadith that makes her free only after the master's death, thus she retains value during his lifetime. The practical difference (ثمرة) is in cases of guarantee: Abu Hanifa says no guarantee is due if someone frees her because she had no value, while the Sahibayn say guarantee is due for half her value.

Key Terms
تقوم (taqawwum): Having a market value or being considered as property for compensation purposes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, what is the market value of an umm walad?
A) Full value of a regular slave
B) One-third the value of a regular slave
C) No value
D) Half the value of a regular slave

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's relied-upon position is that an umm walad has no market value due to her impending freedom upon the master's death.

Freeing Joint Umm Walad: Guarantee Dispute
Ruling on guarantee when one co-owner frees the joint umm walad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on guarantee when a co-owner frees a joint umm walad, and explain the reasoning behind Abu Hanifa's view versus the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
No guarantee for freeing a joint umm walad: she is guarded for lineage, not trade value.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a co-owner who frees a jointly owned umm walad must compensate the other partner. The disagreement hinges on whether the umm walad has market value (māliyya). Abu Hanifa holds she is not subject to valuation because she is guarded for lineage; the Sahibayn argue she retains value like a mudabbir.

Guided Path
1
State the case
Identify the fact pattern: two co-owners, one frees the joint umm walad while wealthy. What is the legal question?
2
Identify the two positions
Abu Hanifa says no guarantee; Sahibayn say guarantee half value. Write them clearly.
3
Analyze the core reasoning
Abu Hanifa: taqawwum (value) depends on ihraz for trade; umm walad is ihraz for lineage. Sahibayn: benefits are derivable, so she has value; non-saleability does not negate (analogy to mudabbir).
Focus on the distinction in ihraz.
4
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical differences: ghasp (usurpation) and death of one co-owner. Apply each position to these scenarios.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text presents Abu Hanifa's view as primary; the mufta bihi is no guarantee. Why might his view be preferred?
Consider consistency with the umm walad's unique status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلا يضمن بإعتاقها [ أي بإعتاق أم الولد بأن ولدت فادعياه وصارت أم ولد لهما فأعتقها أحدهما لم يضمن. (ط)] أي إن كانت أم ولد بينهما، فأعتقها أحدهما موسراً فلا ضمان عليه عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأن مالية أم الولد غير متقومة عنده، وقالا يضمن نصف قيمتها؛ إذ هي عندهما؛ لأنه ينتفع بها وطياً وإجارة واستخداماً وهذا دلالة التقوم، وبامتناع بيعها لا يسقط تقومها كما في المدبر، ولأبي حنيفة: أن التقوم بالإحراز وهي محرزة للنسب لا للتقوم، والإحراز بالتقوم تابع للإحراز بالنسب، فكانت محرزة إحراز المنكوحات لا إحراز المملوكات فلا يعتبر الإحراز للتقوم، ومن ثمرة الخلاف ما إذا غصبها غاصب، فهلكت عنده، لم يضمن خلافاً لهما، ومنها: إذا مات أحد الموليين عتقت عنده، ولم تسع، وعندهما: تسعى في نصف قيمتها. رمز الحقائق: ۳۲۹/۱] مستخلص) لاثنين أي قال المولى لاثنين منهم في الصحة (عيني) وكرر: أي قوله أحد كما حر، فما دام يؤمر بالبيان. (ط)
So he does not guarantee by freeing her. [i.e., by freeing the umm walad: if she gave birth and they both claimed her and she became umm walad for both, then one of them freed her while wealthy, he is not liable (according to Abu Hanifa).] That is, if she is umm walad between them, and one of them freed her while wealthy, there is no guarantee upon him according to Abu Hanifa, because the property value of the umm walad is not considered marketable according to him. And they (the Sahibayn) said: He guarantees half her value, because according to them she has value, as one benefits from her by intercourse, hire, and use, and this indicates value. And the prohibition of her sale does not negate her value, as in the case of the mudabbir. For Abu Hanifa: value depends on being guarded (ihraz) for trade, but she is guarded for lineage, not for value. Guarding for value is subsidiary to guarding for lineage. So she is guarded like wives, not like slaves, so guarding for value is not considered. Among the practical differences: if a usurper seizes her and she perishes with him, according to Abu Hanifa he does not guarantee, contrary to them. Also, if one of the two masters dies, according to Abu Hanifa she becomes free without sa'yah; according to them, she must work for half her value. [Reference: Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1/329]
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage applies the dispute about the value of the umm walad to the specific case of guarantee. If a joint umm walad (two owners) is freed by one of them, does he owe the other partner compensation? According to Imam Abu Hanifa, no, because the umm walad has no market value (malia). The two Sahibayn disagree and rule that he must guarantee half her value, as she is property that yields benefit. The text elaborates the reasoning: Abu Hanifa argues that value (taqawwum) is determined by the slave being guarded (muhraz) for trade, but the umm walad is guarded for lineage (through her child). Her guarding is like that of wives, not like that of ordinary slaves. Therefore, she is not subject to valuation. The practical consequences (thamar) are listed: if someone usurps her and she dies, no compensation according to Abu Hanifa; if one co-owner dies, she becomes fully free without sa'yah according to Abu Hanifa, while the Sahibayn require sa'yah for half value.

Key Terms
إحراز (iḥrāz): Guarding or holding property for a purpose; here distinguishing between guarding for trade vs. for lineage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if one of two co-owners frees a joint umm walad, what guarantee is due?
A) Guarantee for half her value
B) No guarantee
C) Guarantee for full value
D) Guarantee for one-third her value

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa's ruling that no guarantee is due upon freeing a joint umm walad rests on the principle that she is guarded for lineage, not trade value, making her non-mutaqawwima for such disputes.

Actions that Serve as Clarification for Ambiguous Emancipation
Listing of actions that constitute a bayān for ambiguous emancipation and dispute on waṭ'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which actions constitute a bayān in ambiguous emancipation and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether waṭ' without conception is a bayān.

Core Idea
Actions that remove one slave from eligibility automatically free the other; waṭ' without conception is disputed.

When a master says 'one of you is free' without specifying, the emancipation is ambiguous. Certain actions by the master with one of the slaves can clarify which one was intended. This lesson explores the list of actions that serve as such clarification (bayān) and examines the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two companions regarding whether sexual intercourse without conception qualifies as a bayān.

Guided Path
1
Understand ambiguous emancipation
The master says 'one of you is free' without specifying which slave. This creates a state of ambiguity (mubham).
The two slaves are considered equal in potential for freedom.
2
Identify the general rule
Any action that definitively removes one slave from the pool (e.g., death, sale, manumission) automatically frees the other because the competitor is gone.
This is the basis for the list of actions.
3
Learn the ikhbār vs. inshā’ distinction
Statements of fact (ikhbār) like 'one of you is my son' are not clarification because they can apply to the dead; emancipation is an act of creation (inshā') that only applies to the living.
This explains why death of a slave does not clarify if the master merely claimed parenthood.
4
Examine the list of valid bayān actions
The passage lists many actions: sale, death, tadbīr, kitābah, istīlād, taḥrīm, gift, charity, bequest, marriage, offering for sale, pledge.
All these actions remove one slave from the pool of potential freed slaves.
5
Analyze the dispute on waṭ’
Abu Hanifa: waṭ' without conception is not a bayān. Sahibayn: it is a bayān. Compare their proofs and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.
The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa, the other slave is not freed; under Sahibayn, she is.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(ط) قسم الثلث على هذا بأن يجعل كل عبد سبعة أسهم كسهام العتق (عيني) والبيع إلخ [مبتدأ أي عبديه ولو فاسداً فيما إذا قال: أحدكما حر من غير عين (عيني)] إلى قوله: "بيان في العتق المبهم" أي البيع مطلقاً سواء كان صحيحاً أو فاسداً، أو مع القبض أو بدونه، ومشروطاً بشرط الخيار أو بدونه، والموت أي أحدهما ولو بالقتل من المولى أو من أجنبي، ينبغي أن يكون قتل العبد نفسه كذلك، واحترز به عن قطع اليد فإنه لا يكون بياناً، والتدبير، وكذا الكتابة وتعليق أحدهما بالشرط، وكذا الاستيلاد والتحريم يعم المنجز والمعلق كقوله لأحدهما: إن دخلت الدار فأنت حر والهبة ولو بدون القبض، وكذا الصدقة بيان لقوله: أحدكما حر من غير عين؛ لأن هذا الكلام أوجب عتقاً متردداً بينهما فكانا فيه سواء. يصح فإذا مات أحدهما أو باعه أو أعتقه أو دبره أو وهبه تعين الآخر للعتق من غير تعيين لزوال المزاحم، ولا يرد على هذا ما إذا قال الغلامين: أحدهما ابني، أو قال الجاريتين: إحداهما أم ولدي فمات أحدهما، لا يتعين الباقي للعتق ولا للاستيلاد؛ لأن هذا إخبار عن أمر كائن، والإخبار يصح في الحي والميت، بخلاف الإنشاء حيث لا إلا في الحي، والبيان في حكم الإنشاء، فلا يصح إلا في المحل، وهو الحي. رمز الحقائق: ۳۳۱] (فتح) والموت أي موت أحد عبديه في الصورة المذكورة والتحرير: أي تحرير أحدهما في الصورة المذكورة. (عيني) والتدبير أي تدبير أحدهما كذلك ولو مقيدا. (ط) والهبة: أي هبة أحدهما والصدقة والإيصاء والتزويج والعرض على البيع والرهن. (ط) المبهم: وهو ما ذكر من قوله أحدكما حر من غير عين، أي إذا فعل شيئاً مما ذكر بأحدهما تعين الآخر للحرية. (ط، عيني) لا الوطء: أي ليس الوطء بدون العلوق بياناً في العتق المبهم، صورته: إذا كانت له أمتان فقال: إحداهما حرة من غير تعيين، ثم وطئ إحداهما لا يكون وطؤها بياناً الأخرى عند أبي حنيفة وقالا تعتق الأخرى؛ لأن الوطء لا يحل إلا في الملك، فصار الإقدام عليه دليل الاستيفاء، حتى لا تعتق
The sale of one in illness: i.e., in the terminal illness of the master, and the third is insufficient for them, and the heirs do not give permission, and their values are equal. (Ṭāḥāwī) He divided the third according to this by making each slave seven shares like the shares of emancipation ('Aynī). And the sale etc. [beginning: i.e., one of his two slaves, even if [the sale] is invalid (fāsid), in the case where he said: 'One of you is free' without specification ('Aynī)] up to his saying: 'clarification (bayān) in ambiguous emancipation.' That is: sale absolutely, whether valid or invalid, with or without possession, with or without a stipulation of option; and death i.e., the death of one of them, even by killing by the master or a third party, and it includes the slave killing himself similarly; and he excludes cutting off a hand, for it is not a clarification; and tadbīr, and similarly kitābah and the suspension of one of them on a condition, and similarly istīlād and taḥrīm (making haram) whether immediate or suspended, like saying to one: 'If you enter the house, you are free'; and gift (hibah) even without possession; and similarly charity (ṣadaqah) is a clarification for the saying 'one of you is free' without specification, because this statement necessitated a freedom hesitated between them, so they were equal in it. It is valid. For if one of them dies, or he sells him, or frees him, or makes him a mudabbar, or gifts him, then the other becomes determined for freedom without needing specification, due to the removal of the competitor. And this is not refuted by the case where he says about two boys: 'One of them is my son,' or says about two slave-girls: 'One of them is the mother of my child,' then one of them dies, the survivor does not become determined for freedom or for istīlād; because this is informing about a matter that exists, and informing is valid regarding the living and the dead, unlike construction (inshā'), which is only [valid] in the living, and clarification is considered as construction, so it is only valid regarding the subject, which is the living. (Rumūz al-Ḥaqā'iq: 331) (Fatḥ) And death: i.e., the death of one of his two slaves in the mentioned scenario. And taḥrīr: i.e., freeing one of them in the mentioned scenario. ('Aynī) And tadbīr: i.e., making one of them a mudabbar similarly, even if restricted. (Ṭāḥāwī) And hibah: i.e., gifting one of them, and charity, and bequest, and marriage, and offering for sale, and pledge (rahn). (Ṭāḥāwī) The ambiguous (mubham): it is what was mentioned from his saying 'one of you is free' without specification, i.e., if he does any of the mentioned actions with one of them, the other becomes determined for freedom. (Ṭāḥāwī, 'Aynī) Not sexual intercourse (waṭ'): i.e., sexual intercourse without impregnation is not a clarification in ambiguous emancipation. Its form: if he has two female slaves and says: 'One of you is free' without specification, then he had intercourse with one of them, his intercourse with her is not a clarification of the other according to Abu Hanifa, and they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: the other becomes free. Because intercourse is not permissible except in ownership, so undertaking it becomes evidence of exercising ownership, so that the other is not freed.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage clarifies what actions qualify as a 'bayān' (clarification) when a master says 'one of you is free' without specifying. If the master performs certain actions with one of the two slaves, that action indicates his choice, and the other slave is automatically freed. The actions listed include: sale (even invalid), death, manumission, tadbīr (contract of emancipation after death), gift, charity, bequest, marriage, offering for sale, pledge, etc. The text distinguishes between informing (ikhbār) and creating (inshā'): if the master says 'one of you is my son', death of one does not determine the other, because that is a statement of fact that can apply to the dead. But the ambiguous emancipation is an act of creation (inshā') that only operates on the living, so once one slave becomes unavailable (by death or transfer), the other is automatically free. The passage then addresses a dispute: according to Abu Hanifa, sexual intercourse (waṭ') without conception is NOT a clarification; but Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say it is a clarification and the other slave becomes free. The reasoning: intercourse is only lawful in one's own property, so engaging in it indicates that the master considers that slave as his exclusive property, which implies that the other is free. Abu Hanifa holds that intercourse without conception is not definitive enough to indicate exclusive ownership, possibly because it could be done mistakenly or as a foreplay.

Key Terms
بيان (bayān): An action or event that clarifies which slave was intended in an ambiguous emancipation statement.
عتق مبهم ('itq mubham): An emancipation that is ambiguous because the master said 'one of you is free' without specifying.
وطء (waṭ'): Sexual intercourse with a female slave, without conception.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, it clarifies the choice.
B) No, it is not a clarification.
C) It is a clarification only if followed by a verbal statement.
D) It is a clarification only if the slave is a concubine (umm walad).

Key Takeaway
Actions that remove one slave from eligibility (sale, death, etc.) clarify ambiguous emancipation; waṭ' without conception is within the Hanafi school, with the Sahibayn's view being the operative one.

Clarification (Bayān) in Ambiguous Emancipation: The Dispute on Intercourse
Listing actions that serve as bayān and dispute on intercourse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on whether intercourse serves as bayān in ambiguous emancipation, explain the reasoning of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and apply the ruling to analogous cases.

Core Idea
Intercourse can clarify ambiguous emancipation only if it indicates retention of ownership; the Hanafi fatwa follows the Sahibayn.

When a master ambiguously frees one of two slaves, certain acts resolve the ambiguity. This lesson examines the list of clarifying acts and focuses on the disputed case of intercourse. Understanding the reasoning behind the ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to infer legal intent from circumstantial evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts that serve as bayān
From the passage, list the actions that are explicitly said to be clarification: sale, death, freeing, tadbīr, and gift. Note that these acts, when performed on one slave, determine that the other is the one intended for freedom.
These acts are considered strong indicators of the master's intent.
2
Understand the concept of bayān in ʿitq mubham
Bayān here means an event or action that resolves the ambiguity created by the master's unspecific statement. The act itself, not a verbal declaration, clarifies which slave is freed.
This is a practical application of bayān in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Locate the disputed act (watʾ) and the two positions
The passage states that according to Abu Hanifa, intercourse without pregnancy is not bayān. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is bayān. The fatwa is given on the Sahibayn's view.
The disagreement is over the legal effect of an ambiguous action.
4
Analyze the dalīl of the Sahibayn
Their proof: 'Intercourse is not permissible except in one's own property.' Therefore, by engaging in it, the master indicates that the woman is his property, so the other must be the freed one.
This is an istidlāl bil-qarīnah (inference from circumstantial evidence).
5
Note the thamarah al-khilāf and the muftā bihī
The practical difference: if watʾ is considered bayān, the other slave becomes free immediately. If not, the ambiguity remains. The relied-upon fatwa adopts the Sahibayn's view.
This ruling only applies when the divorce is irrevocable (bāʾin) or before consummation, as the passage later clarifies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والبيع والموت والتحرير والتدبير والهبة بيان في العتق المبهم. لا الوطء: أي ليس الوطء بدون العلوق بياناً في العتق المبهم، صورته: إذا كانت له أمتان فقال: إحداهما حرة من غير تعيين، ثم وطئ إحداهما لا يكون وطؤها بياناً الأخرى عند أبي حنيفة وقالا تعتق الأخرى؛ لأن الوطء لا يحل إلا في الملك، فصار الإقدام عليه دليل الاستيفاء، حتى لا تعتق. ثم بيان في الطلاق المبهم: يعني من قال لامرأتيه إحداكما طالق، فوطئ إحداهما وماتت، طلقت الأخرى بالاتفاق، ولابد أن يكون الطلاق بائناً أو قبل الدخول، أما لو كان رجعياً لا يكون الوطء بياناً لطلاق الأخرى؛ لحل وطء المطلقة الرجعية، أما في الوطء؛ فلان المقصود الأصلي من النكاح الولد وقصد الولد بالوطء يدل على استبقاء الملك في الموطوءة صيانة للولد، أما في الأمة فالمقصود من الوطء قضاء الشهوة دون الولد، فلا يدل على استبقاء الملك، وأما في موت إحداهما؛ فلأن بيان محل الطلاق إنشاء الطلاق من وجه، فلابد له من محل، وبعد الموت لم تبق محلاً للطلاق أصلاً فتعينت الأخرى للطلاق.
And sale, death, freeing, tadbir, and gift are clarification in ambiguous emancipation. Not intercourse: meaning intercourse without pregnancy is not clarification in ambiguous emancipation. Its form: If he has two slave women and says 'One of you is free' without specification, then he has intercourse with one of them, his intercourse with her is not clarification of the other according to Abu Hanifa, and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say the other becomes free because intercourse is not permissible except in ownership, so undertaking it becomes evidence of retention (of ownership), so that (the other) does not become free. Then clarification in ambiguous divorce: meaning whoever said to his two wives 'One of you is divorced' then he had intercourse with one of them and she died, the other becomes divorced by agreement. And it is necessary that the divorce be irrevocable (ba'in) or before consummation. As for if it were revocable (raj'i), intercourse does not become clarification for the other's divorce because revocable divorcee's intercourse is permissible. As for intercourse (in the case of divorce), because the primary aim of marriage is offspring, and the intention of offspring through intercourse indicates retention of ownership in the one with whom intercourse is had for the preservation of the child. As for the slave woman, the aim of intercourse is gratification of desire without offspring, so it does not indicate retention of ownership. And as for the death of one of them, because the clarification of the place of divorce is a kind of creation of divorce, so it requires a place, and after death there remains no locus for divorce at all, so the other becomes determined for divorce.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage deals with the rules of bayān (clarification) in ambiguous emancipation (al-ʿitq al-mubham), where a master says 'one of you is free' without specifying. The text first lists actions that serve as bayān: sale, death, freeing, tadbir (suspensive emancipation upon death), and gift. These acts, when performed on one of the slaves, determine that the other is the one intended for freedom. The key exception is intercourse (watʾ) without pregnancy. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, intercourse without impregnation is not a bayān, because its purpose is merely gratification, not indicating retention of ownership for offspring. However, his two companions Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that intercourse does serve as bayān, because intercourse is only permissible in one's own property; performing it indicates that the master considers the woman his property, thereby confirming that the other is the intended free person. The fatwa (mufta bihi) is given on the opinion of the Sahibayn. The passage then draws a parallel with ambiguous divorce: if a man says 'one of you is divorced' and then has intercourse with one and she dies, the other becomes divorced by consensus, but only if the divorce was irrevocable or before consummation. The rationale distinguishes between intercourse for offspring (stronger indication of retention) and for pleasure (weaker). This shows the nuanced Hanafi approach to inferring intent from actions.

Key Terms
العتق المبهم (al-ʿitq al-mubham): Emancipation that is ambiguous, as when a master says 'one of you is free' without specifying which slave.
البيان (al-bayān): An act or event that resolves the ambiguity by indicating which slave is intended for freedom.
الوطء (al-watʾ): Sexual intercourse; in this context, with a slave woman without resulting pregnancy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is never a clarification.
B) It is a clarification only if pregnancy results.
C) It is a clarification, so the other slave becomes free.
D) It is a clarification only if the master explicitly states his intention.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi view is that intercourse with one of two ambiguously owned slave women serves as clarification, freeing the other.

Conditional Emancipation on Firstborn Child: Six Scenarios
Explaining ruling and six scenarios when order of birth is unknown

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on twins born after a conditional emancipation when order is unknown, and apply the evidentiary rules to determine the freedom status in different claim scenarios.

Core Idea
Uncertain order of birth creates half-freedom for mother and female; male remains enslaved.

In conditional emancipation, the exact moment of condition fulfillment is critical. When a master conditions his slave woman's freedom on her firstborn being male, and she delivers twins with unknown order, Hanafi fiqh provides a nuanced ruling. This lesson walks through the base ruling and six scenarios that depend on claims, evidence, and oaths.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditional emancipation
Recognize that the master's statement creates a suspended emancipation: the mother becomes free only if the condition (first child is male) is met.
2
Determine the base ruling under uncertainty
When twins are born and order unknown, the male is always enslaved because he is born before the condition is fulfilled; the mother and female are half-free due to uncertainty, each required to perform sa'y (work) for half their value.
This is the ruling when order is unknown and no other claims are made.
3
Map the six scenarios
The text lists six procedural scenarios based on who claims the male is first, and the reactions of the master and others. For each, the outcome (who becomes free) changes.
Focus on the pattern: the master's denial with oath blocks freedom unless the claimant brings evidence or the master refuses to swear (nukul).
4
Apply the evidentiary rules
Understand the role of qawl (statement), yamin (oath), nukul (refusal to swear), and bayyinah (evidence). The master's oath is given weight because he is denying the condition. Refusal to swear only benefits the claimant who made the claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قال: رجل لأمته إن كان أول ولد تلدينه ذكراً فأنت حرّة، فولدت ذكراً وأنثى ولم يدر الأول، ربّ الذكر وعتق نصف الأم والأنثى، والاحتياط أي منهما أي بقي رقيقاً ترك. ثم ذكر الستة أوجه: الأول أنه لم يدر الأول والجواب ما ذكرنا والثاني: أن تدعي الأم أن الغلام أول وأنكر المولى ذلك وقال: الأول وهي صغيرة، فالقول للمولى مع يمينه؛ لأنه ينكر شرط العتق ويحلف على عدم علمه؛ لأنه فعل البنت هي الغير، فإذا حلف لم يعتق واحد منهما إلا أن تقيم الأم البينة بعد ذلك على أنها ولدت الغلام أولا. فإن نكل عتقت البنت والأم؛ لأن النكول حجة ضرورية فلا يتعدى، والثالث: أن يوجد التصادق بأن الغلام هو الأول، فتعتق الأم والبنت ويرق الغلام؛ لأنه لاحظ له من العتق بحال، والرابع: أن يوجد التصادق بأن البنت هي الأولى، فلا أحد يعتق منهم، والخامس: أن تدعي الأم بأن الغلام هو الأول، ولم تدع البنت وهي كبيرة، فيحلف المولى، فإن حلف لم يعتق واحد منهم، وإن نكل عتقت الأم دون البنت، والسادس: أن تدعي البنت، وهي كبيرة، أن الغلام هو الأول، ولم تدع الأم، فتعتق البنت إذا نكل دون الأم. والأنثى أي ونصف الأنثى، وسعي كل منهما في نصف قيمته.
And if a man said to his slave woman: 'If the first child you give birth to is a male, then you are free,' and she gave birth to a male and a female and it is not known which was first, the male is withheld (remains enslaved) and half of the mother and the female become free, and the precaution (al-ihtiyat) meaning from them (i.e., each) remains enslaved (if precaution is taken) is left. Then he mentioned the six aspects: First, that he does not know which was first, and the answer is what we mentioned. Second, that the mother claims the male was first and the master denies that and says: the first is the female, and she is a minor (i.e., the female?), then the statement is with the master with his oath because he denies the condition of emancipation and swears on his lack of knowledge, because he (the master) action regarding the female is (?)… So if he swears, neither becomes free unless the mother then establishes evidence that she gave birth to the male first. If he refuses (nukul), the female and mother become free because nukul is a necessary proof but does not extend beyond. Third, that they agree that the male is first, then the mother and female become free and the male remains enslaved because he has no share in freedom in any case. Fourth, that they agree that the female is first, then none become free. Fifth, that the mother claims the male is first, and the female (who is adult) does not claim, then the master swears; if he swears, none become free; if he refuses, the mother becomes free without the female. Sixth, that the female (adult) claims the male is first, and the mother does not claim, then the female becomes free if he refuses without the mother. And 'the female' means half of the female, and each of them works (sa'y) for half of her value.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage addresses conditional emancipation (al-ʿitq al-muʿallaq) where the master says to his slave woman: 'If the first child you give birth to is a male, you are free.' She then gives birth to twins, a male and a female, and the order of birth is unknown. The ruling is that the male remains enslaved because he is born before the condition is fulfilled (the mother becomes free only after his birth, so he is not born free). The mother and the female each become half-free because there is uncertainty: half the time the male is first, half the time the female is first. Each must work (sa'y) to pay half their value to the master. The text then details six scenarios based on who claims what and whether there is evidence or refusal to swear (nukul). These scenarios show how the burden of proof and the legal consequences vary. The core principle is that the condition attached to emancipation creates a suspense, and the outcome depends on whether the condition is proven to have occurred. The ruling demonstrates the Hanafi approach to resolving uncertainty in conditional contracts.

Key Terms
العتق المعلق (al-ʿitq al-muʿallaq): Emancipation that is conditional upon a future event occurring.
أول ولد (awwalu walad): The first child born; in this case, specified as a male.
السعي (al-saʿy): The requirement for a partially freed slave to work to earn money to pay the remaining portion of their value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where the master says 'if first child is male you are free' and twins (male and female) are born with unknown order, what is the status of the male child?
A) He is free because his mother is free.
B) He is half-free like the mother and female.
C) He remains a slave.
D) He is free if the mother claims he is first.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when the order of birth is unknown after a conditional emancipation, the male remains enslaved, the mother and female become half-free, and detailed evidentiary rules determine freedom in various claim scenarios.

Ruling on Ambiguous Manumission with Twin Births
Ruling with proof and analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a master says 'the first child if male is free' and twins of opposite sexes are born with unknown order, and explain the legal reasoning involving bayan and istibqa.

Core Idea
When order unknown, half of mother and daughter freed; male remains slave because he is the condition.

This lesson explores a case of ambiguous manumission: a master conditions freedom on the birth of a male child. When twins are born and order is unknown, the Hanafi school applies a half-free ruling based on precaution. We will trace the reasoning and compare to ambiguous divorce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition and ambiguity
The master says 'the first child you give birth to, if male, you are free.' Twins are born (male and female) and the birth order is unknown. This creates an ambiguous situation.
The condition is suspended on a future event.
2
Determine the ruling for each individual
The male remains a slave in all states. The mother and female are half-free each: half of each is freed, and they must pay half their value to the master.
This is the fatwa position of the Sahibayn.
3
Understand the concept of bayan (clarification)
Ambiguous manumission requires clarification (bayan) to take effect. Until clarified, the default is that all remain slaves. Here, the ambiguity is partially resolved by considering the possibilities.
Bayan can occur through actions or statements.
4
Analyze the proof: why intercourse does not indicate retention
In the case of a wife, intercourse indicates intention to retain (istibqa') because the primary purpose of marriage is offspring. For a slave-girl, intercourse is for desire, not offspring, so it does not clarify the ambiguity.
This is based on qiyas with ambiguous divorce.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute and fatwa position
Abu Hanifa held that both mother and female remain slaves entirely due to precaution. The Sahibayn and the majority (including Shafi'i and Malik) hold that half are freed. Fatwa is given according to the Sahibayn.
The text states 'wa bihi yufta'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قال: أول ولد تلدينه ذكراً فأنت حرّة، فولدت ذكراً وأنثى و لم يدر الأول، ربّ الذكر وعتق نصف الأم والأنثى، الاحتياط أي منهما أي بقي رقيقاً ترك كما إذا وطئ إحدى المرأتين الطلاق المبهم. رمز الحقائق: ۳۳۱/۱] وكما لو علقت منه، وإن الملك ثابت فيهما؛ ولهذا كان له أن يستخدمهما، وكان له الأرش إذا جني عليهما، والمهر إذا وطئها بشبهة؛ لأن العتق المبهم معلق بالبيان والمعلق بالشرط لا ينزل قبله والوطء كالاستخدام؛ لأنه لقضاء الشهوة في الأمة لا لطلب الولد فلا يراد به الاستبقاء، وقول الشافعي ومالك مثل قولهما، وبه يفتى ولا يفتى بقول الإمام لما فيه من أن الإمام ناظر إلى الاحتياط في أكثر المسائل. (فتح) مع بيان في الطلاق المبهم: يعني من قال لامرأتيه إحداكما طالق، فوطئ إحداهما وماتت، طلقت الأخرى بالاتفاق، ولابد أن يكون الطلاق بائناً أو قبل الدخول، أما لو كان رجعياً لا يكون الوطء بياناً لطلاق الأخرى؛ لحل وطء المطلقة الرجعية، أما في الوطء؛ فلان المقصود الأصلي من النكاح الولد وقصد الولد بالوطء يدل على استبقاء الملك في الموطوءة صيانة للولد، أما في الأمة فالمقصود من الوطء قضاء الشهوة دون الولد، فلا يدل على استبقاء الملك، وأما في موت إحداهما؛ فلأن بيان محل الطلاق إنشاء الطلاق من وجه، فلابد له من محل، وبعد الموت لم تبق محلاً للطلاق أصلاً فتعينت الأخرى للطلاق. (مستخلص، فتح) ولو قال: رجل لأمته إن كان أول إلخ. (ط) عيني) وعتق نصف الأم والأنثى: لأن كل واحدة منهما تعتق في حال وهو ما إذا ولدت الغلام أولاً ، فالأم بالشرط والجارية بالتبعية؛ إذ الأم عتقت قبل ولادتها، وترق في حال وهو ما إذا ولدت الجارية أولاً؛ لعدم الشرط، فيعتق نصف كل واحدة منهما، وتسعى في النصف، وأما الغلام فيرق في الحالين؛ لأن ولادته شرط لحرية الأم، فتعتق بعد ولادته فلا يتبعها، وهذه المسألة تتصور على ستة أوجه الأول أنه لم يدر الأول والجواب ما ذكرنا والثاني: أن تدعي الأم أن الغلام أول وأنكر المولى ذلك وقال: الأول وهي صغيرة، فالقول للمولى مع يمينه ؛ لأنه ينكر شرط العتق ويحلف على عدم علمه؛ لأنه فعل البنت هي الغير، فإذا حلف لم يعتق واحد منهما إلا أن تقيم الأم البينة بعد ذلك على أنها ولدت الغلام أولا. فإن نكل عتقت البنت والأم؛ لأن النكول حجة ضرورية فلا يتعدى، والثالث: أن يوجد التصادق بأن الغلام هو الأول، فتعتق الأم والبنت ويرق الغلام؛ لأنه لاحظ له من العتق بحال، والرابع: أن يوجد التصادق بأن البنت هي الأولى، فلا أحد يعتق منهم، والخامس : أن تدعي الأم بأن الغلام هو الأول، ولم تدع البنت وهي كبيرة، فيحلف المولى، فإن حلف لم يعتق واحد منهم، وإن نكل عتقت الأم دون البنت، والسادس: أن تدعي البنت، وهي كبيرة، أن الغلام هو الأول، ولم تدع الأم، فتعتق البنت إذا نكل دون الأم رمز الحقائق: ۳۳۱/۱] (مستخلص) والأنثى أي ونصف الأنثى، وسعي كل منهما في نصف قيمته.
And if he said: 'The first child you give birth to, if male, you are free,' and she gave birth to a male and a female and it is not known which was first, the male remains a slave and half of the mother and the female are freed, as a precaution. [Commentary: 'of which one remains a slave' as when he had intercourse with one of two wives in ambiguous divorce. And likewise if she became pregnant from him, and ownership is confirmed in both; thus he may use them both, and he is entitled to compensation if they are injured, and the dower if he has intercourse with her under a semblance of right; because ambiguous manumission is suspended on clarification, and what is suspended on a condition does not occur before it, and intercourse is like use; because it is for satisfying desire in a slave-girl, not for seeking offspring, so it does not indicate retention. The statement of al-Shafi'i and Malik is like theirs (the two companions), and according to it fatwa is given, not according to the Imam's statement, because the Imam considered precaution in most issues. (Fath) With an explanation of ambiguous divorce: meaning whoever said to his two wives 'one of you is divorced,' and he had intercourse with one and she died, the other is divorced by consensus, and it must be a irrevocable divorce or before consummation, but if it is a revocable divorce, intercourse does not clarify the divorce of the other because intercourse with a revocably divorced woman is permissible. As for intercourse [in the case of a wife], the primary purpose of marriage is offspring, and intending offspring by intercourse indicates retention of ownership in the one with whom intercourse occurred to protect the offspring. As for a slave-girl, the purpose of intercourse is satisfying desire, not offspring, so it does not indicate retention. As for the death of one [wife], because clarifying the subject of divorce is creating divorce in a sense, so it must have a subject, and after death there is no subject for divorce at all, so the other is determined for divorce. (Mustakhlas, Fath) And if a man said to his slave-girl 'If the first... etc.' (Ayni) And half of the mother and the female are freed because each of them is free in one state, which is when she gave birth to the male first: the mother by the condition and the female by following; since the mother became free before her birth. And each is a slave in one state, which is when she gave birth to the female first, due to lack of condition, so half of each is freed, and she [the slave-girl] must pay for the half. As for the male, he remains a slave in both states because his birth is a condition for the mother's freedom, so she becomes free after his birth, so he does not follow her. This issue has six aspects: first: he does not know the first, and the answer is what we mentioned. Second: the mother claims that the male was first and the master denies and says the first was the female, and she is young. Then the statement is the master's with his oath because he denies the condition of freedom and swears on his lack of knowledge; because the act is the other's. If he swears, none are freed unless the mother brings proof after that that she gave birth to the male first. If he refuses to swear, the daughter and mother are freed because refusal is a necessary proof and does not extend beyond. Third: it is agreed that the male is first, then the mother and daughter are freed and the male remains a slave because he has no share in freedom in any state. Fourth: it is agreed that the female is first, then none of them are freed. Fifth: the mother claims the male is first, and the daughter does not claim and she is an adult, then the master swears. If he swears, none are freed; if he refuses, the mother is freed but not the daughter. Sixth: the daughter, being adult, claims the male is first, and the mother does not claim, then the daughter is freed if he refuses, not the mother. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 331/1, Mustakhlas) And the female: meaning half the female, and each of them must pay half of her value.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on a specific condition of ambiguous manumission ('itq mubham) and explains the legal reasoning (ta'lil) and the required clarification (bayan). The case: a man says to his slave-girl, 'The first child you give birth to, if male, you are free.' She gives birth to twins of opposite sexes, but the order is unknown. The ruling: the male remains a slave, and the mother and female are half-free each; each must pay half their value to the master. This is based on precaution (ihtiyat). The text then compares this to ambiguous divorce (talaq mubham) to illustrate the principle of clarification by intercourse. In divorce, intercourse with one wife clarifies that she is not the one divorced, because the intention of offspring indicates retention. But with a slave-girl, intercourse is only for desire, not offspring, so it does not indicate retention. Therefore, in the slave-girl case, intercourse does not clarify the ambiguity. The author notes that Shafi'i and Malik agree with Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) on this ruling, and that fatwa is given according to them, not according to Abu Hanifa, who favored precaution. The six scenarios cover various possibilities of claims and evidence, outlining who is freed based on claims, oaths, and proof. This demonstrates the Hanafi method of applying qiyas (analogy) and istihsan (juristic preference) in rulings of ambiguous conditions.

Key Terms
العتق المبهم (al-'itq al-mubham): Manumission that is ambiguous, where the subject is not specified, such as 'one of my slaves is free.'
البيان (al-bayan): Clarification or specification of an ambiguous matter, such as determining which slave is meant.
الاستبقاء (al-istibqa'): Intention to retain ownership, indicated by acts that seek offspring or benefit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling when a master says 'the first child if male is free' and twins of opposite sexes are born with unknown order?
A) All three are free because a male child was born.
B) The mother and male are free; the female remains a slave.
C) The male remains a slave, and half of the mother and female are freed.
D) None are freed until the master clarifies the ambiguity.

Key Takeaway
In ambiguous manumission with unknown birth order, half-freedom is granted to the mother and female twin, while the male remains a slave.

The Six Scenarios of Claims and Oaths in Ambiguous Manumission
Procedural expansion: six cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the legal status of the mother, daughter, and male slave in each of the six scenarios based on claims, oaths, and evidence.

Core Idea
The master's word is accepted unless the mother provides proof; refusal to swear can lead to freedom.

This lesson details the procedural rules when a dispute arises about the birth order. The six scenarios cover all possibilities of who claims what, and the outcome differs based on oaths and evidence.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the six possible scenarios
The text enumerates six situations based on who claims the male was born first (mother, daughter, both, or none) and whether the master denies or agrees.
Scenario 1 is the default where no one knows the order.
2
For each scenario, identify who takes an oath and the consequence
The master is generally believed with an oath if he denies knowledge. If he refuses to swear (nukul), the claimant's statement is accepted partially.
Nukul only frees the party who made the claim.
3
Understand the role of evidence
If the mother brings proof that the male was first, that overrides the master's oath. Evidence is given priority over oaths.
The text mentions 'beyyina' (proof) as a deciding factor.
4
Apply to each scenario to determine who is freed
Go through scenarios 2-6: in each, identify the claimants, the master's response, and the outcome based on oath or nukul.
Use the text's descriptions for precise rulings.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on a specific condition of ambiguous manumission ('itq mubham) and explains the legal reasoning (ta'lil) and the required clarification (bayan). The case: a man says to his slave-girl, 'The first child you give birth to, if male, you are free.' She gives birth to twins of opposite sexes, but the order is unknown. The ruling: the male remains a slave, and the mother and female are half-free each; each must pay half their value to the master. This is based on precaution (ihtiyat). The text then compares this to ambiguous divorce (talaq mubham) to illustrate the principle of clarification by intercourse. In divorce, intercourse with one wife clarifies that she is not the one divorced, because the intention of offspring indicates retention. But with a slave-girl, intercourse is only for desire, not offspring, so it does not indicate retention. Therefore, in the slave-girl case, intercourse does not clarify the ambiguity. The six scenarios cover various possibilities of claims and evidence, outlining who is freed based on claims, oaths, and proof. This demonstrates the Hanafi method of applying qiyas (analogy) and istihsan (juristic preference) in rulings of ambiguous conditions.

Key Terms
العتق المبهم (al-'itq al-mubham): Manumission that is ambiguous, where the subject is not specified, such as 'one of my slaves is free.'
النكول (al-nukul): Refusal to take an oath; in Hanafi law, nukul is considered an admission of the opponent's claim in certain contexts.

Testimony on Ambiguous Manumission: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of testimony for unspecified manumission with exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding testimony on ambiguous manumission, and identify the exceptions where testimony is accepted.

Core Idea
Testimony on ambiguous manumission is invalid unless a claim can be made, except in wills and divorce.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of witness testimony when a man says 'one of my two slaves is free' without specifying which. The disagreement hinges on the nature of manumission: is it a right of the slave (huquq al-'ibad) or a right of Allah (huquq Allah)? This classification determines whether a claim from the slave is required for testimony to be accepted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
Two witnesses testify that a man freed one of his two male or female slaves without specifying which. The question is whether this testimony is valid.
The manumission is mubham (ambiguous).
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and reasoning
Abu Hanifa rules the testimony invalid. For a male slave, manumission is a right of the slave, so a claim from the slave is necessary. Since the slave is unknown, no claim can be made. For a female slave, though no claim is needed, ambiguous manumission is still rejected because it does not make her private parts forbidden immediately.
This is based on the principle that manumission is from huquq al-'ibad.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and reasoning
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad rule the testimony valid and compel the man to free one. They consider manumission a right of Allah, so no claim is required.
They rely on the principle that manumission is from huquq Allah.
4
Identify the exceptions
Testimony is accepted in two cases by consensus: (1) if the manumission is part of a will (during terminal illness) or tadbir (deferred manumission), because the claim effectively comes from the heirs or executor; (2) if it is an ambiguous divorce, because divorce directly involves prohibition of intercourse, which is a right of Allah.
Also, if witnesses testify after death that the man said 'one of you is free' in health, the accepted view is that it is admitted.
5
Analyse the underlying principle
The dispute reduces to whether testimony on a right of a slave requires a claimant (Abu Hanifa) or not (Sahibayn). The exceptions show that when a right of Allah is involved, or when a claimant effectively exists, testimony is accepted.
This is a classic talil (reasoning) based on the nature of rights.

Source Text

باب العبد الذي يعتق بعضه
ولو شهدا أنه حرّر أحد عبديه أو أمتيه ،لغت إلا أن تكون في وصيّة أو طلاق

مبهم.
ولو شهدا إلخ: أي لو شهد رجلان على آخر أنه أعتق أحد عبديه أو إحدى أمتيه، لغت هذه الشهادة عند أبي حنيفة، أما الأولى: فلأن الشهادة على عتق العبد لا تقبل بلا دعوى العبد عنده، ولا دعوى منهم ههنا؛ لكونه مجهولا غير معين، وأما الثانية: فلأن الدعوى وإن لم تكن شرطاً في حق الأمة لكن الشهادة على العتق المبهم مردودة كما في أحد العبدين، وقالا: تقبل، ويؤمر بأن أحدهما، يعتق قالت الثلاثة، والخلاف مبني على أن العتق من حقوق العباد عنده، فتتوقف الشهادة على دعوى العبد، ولا تحقق لها من المملوك فلغت، وعندهما: العتق من حقوق الله تعالى فلم تتوقف، وعتق الأمة وإن لم يتوقف على الدعوى إجماعاً؛ لما فيه من تحريم فرجها على المولى، وهو خالص حقه تعالى فأشبه الطلاق إلا أن العتق المبهم لا يوجب تحريم الفرج عنده على ما مر. (عيني، فتح)
العبدين مبهم
وبه
إلا أن تكون استثناء متصل يعني لغت الشهادة في كل الأحوال إلا في الصورتين الآتيتين. (فتح) في وصية أي تقبل الشهادة لو شهدا أنه أعتق أحد عبديه في مرض موته أو شهدا على تدبيره في صحته أو مرضه وأديا الشهادة في مرض موته أو بعد موته تقبل الشهادة استحساناً، والقياس أن لا تقبل لجهالة المدعى – وهو أحد - ، والاستحسان وجهان أحدهما أن العتق في المرض والتدبير مطلقاً وصية، والخصم فيها إنما هو الموصي؛ لأنه حقه، ونفعه يعود إليه، فتحقق الدعوى من الخلف، وهو الوصي أو الوارث، فكان الموصي مدعياً تقديراً، والثاني: أن العتق بالموت يشيع فيهما، ولهذا يعتق نصف كل واحد منهما، فصار كل واحد خصماً، والأصل في ذلك أن الدعوى من العبد شرط في الشهادة لا العتق عنده لا عندهما كما مر بيانه، ولو شهدا بعد موته أنه قال في صحته أحدكما حر فلا نص فيه، فقيل لا تقبل والأصح أنها تقبل. (عيني، فتح)
أو طلاق مبهم وهذه الصورة الثانية التي تقبل فيها الشهادة إجماعاً أي لو شهد أنه طلق إحدى نسائه تقبل إجماعاً ويجبر الزوج على أن يبين الطلاق المبهم في إحداهن؛ لأن في الطلاق تحريم الفرج وهو حق الله تعالى، فلا يشترط الدعوى وكذلك في الأمة المعينة؛ لأن تحريم فرجها حق الشرع وفيما هو حق الشرع الشهادة تقبل حسبة من غير الدعوى كما في الشهادة برؤية هلال رمضان وحد الزنا وحد شرب الخمر، فإن قيل: فعلى هذا ينبغي أن يكتفى بشهادة الواحد؛ لأن تحريم الفرج أمر ديني فيقبل فيه خبر الواحد وهو فيه حجة تامة، قلنا: خبر الواحد إنما يكون حجة إذا لم يتضمن إزالة حق العبد، وههنا يتضمن إزالة الملك عن الزوج والمولي، فلا يقبل. (مستخلص، فتح)
Chapter on the slave who is partially emancipated. And if two men testify that a man freed one of his two male slaves or one of his two female slaves, it is invalid unless it is in a will or divorce. Meaning: two men against a man? The testimony is ambiguous. 'And if two men testify etc.': meaning if two men testify against another that he freed one of his two male slaves or one of his two female slaves, this testimony is invalid according to Abu Hanifa. As for the first, because testimony on freeing a male slave is not accepted without a claim from the slave according to him, and there is no claim from them here because he is unknown and unspecified. As for the second, because although a claim is not a condition regarding a female slave, testimony on ambiguous manumission is rejected as in the case of one of two male slaves. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: it is accepted, and he is ordered to free one of them. The three (imams) said? The dispute is based on the fact that manumission is from the rights of slaves according to him (Abu Hanifa), so testimony depends on a claim from the slave, and there is no verification from the slave, so it is invalid. According to them (the two), manumission is from the rights of Allah, so it does not depend. And freeing a female slave, although it does not depend on a claim by consensus, because it involves making her private parts forbidden to the master, which is a pure right of Allah, so it resembles divorce, except that ambiguous manumission does not make the private parts forbidden according to him as previously mentioned. (Ayni, Fath) 'Except that it is a connected exception' meaning the testimony is invalid in all cases except the two following images. (Fath) 'In a will': meaning the testimony is accepted if they testify that he freed one of his two slaves in his terminal illness, or they testify about his tadbir (deferred manumission) in health or illness, and they give testimony in his terminal illness or after his death; the testimony is accepted by istihsan. By qiyas it would not be accepted due to ignorance of the defendant – which is one – and istihsan has two aspects: one is that manumission in illness and tadbir absolutely is a will, and the opponent in it is only the testator because it is his right and its benefit returns to him, so the claim is actualized from the successor, who is the executor or heir, and the testator is considered a plaintiff hypothetically. The second is that manumission spreads through both at death, so half of each becomes free, and each becomes a defendant. The principle in that is that a claim from the slave is a condition for testimony, not manumission, according to him (Abu Hanifa) not according to them (the two), as previously explained. If they testify after his death that he said in his health 'one of you is free', there is no text on it; it is said it is not accepted, and the more correct view is that it is accepted. (Ayni, Fath) 'Or ambiguous divorce' – this is the second image in which testimony is accepted by consensus. Meaning if they testify that he divorced one of his wives, it is accepted by consensus, and the husband is compelled to clarify the ambiguous divorce among them, because in divorce there is prohibition of the private parts, which is a right of Allah, so a claim is not necessary. Similarly for a specific female slave, because making her private parts forbidden is a right of the Sharia, and in what is a right of the Sharia, testimony is accepted gratuitously without a claim, as in testimony about sighting the crescent of Ramadan, the hadd for zina, and the hadd for drinking wine. If it is said: accordingly, the testimony of one should suffice, because prohibition of private parts is a religious matter, so the report of one is accepted and it is a complete proof; we say: the report of one is only a proof if it does not entail removal of a right of the slave, and here it entails removal of ownership from the husband and master, so it is not accepted. (Mustakhlas, Fath)
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the validity of witness testimony regarding ambiguous manumission. Abu Hanifa holds that testimony that a man freed one of his two slaves (without specifying which) is invalid because manumission is a right of the slaves, requiring a claim from the slave. Since the slave is unknown here, no claim can be made, so the testimony is invalid. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that manumission is a right of Allah, so no claim is necessary, and the testimony is accepted; the man is ordered to free one of the two. However, there are two exceptions where testimony is accepted even according to Abu Hanifa: (1) if the manumission is in a will (during terminal illness) or a tadbir (deferred manumission), because in those cases the claim is effectively from the heirs or executor; (2) if it is an ambiguous divorce (saying he divorced one of his wives), because divorce makes intercourse unlawful, which is a right of Allah, so no claim is needed. The passage also discusses sub-issues: if witnesses testify after the man's death that he said in health 'one of you is free', the correct view is that it is accepted. The underlying principle is that the basis of the dispute is whether manumission is a right of the slaves or a right of Allah.

Key Terms
عتق مبهم (itq mubham): A manumission where the slave is unspecified, e.g., 'one of my two slaves is free.'
حقوق العباد (huquq al-'ibad): Rights that pertain to individuals, requiring their claim for legal action.
حقوق الله (huquq Allah): Rights that pertain to Allah, where no individual claim is necessary.
تدبير (tadbir): Deferred manumission; a master declares a slave will be free upon the master's death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is testimony on ambiguous manumission of a male slave invalid according to Abu Hanifa?
A) Because manumission is a right of Allah and requires no claim.
B) Because manumission is a right of the slave, and the slave is unknown, so no claim can be made.
C) Because the slave must be present to consent.
D) Because the testimony is based on hearsay.

Key Takeaway
The validity of testimony on ambiguous manumission depends on whether manumission is classified as a right of the slave (requiring a claimant) or a right of Allah (no claimant needed), with exceptions for wills and divorce.

Conditional Emancipation: The Effect of the Word 'Yawma'idh'
Commentary on the legal effect of 'yawma'idh' in conditional emancipation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on conditional emancipation oaths involving the phrase 'yawma'idh' to determine whether after-acquired slaves are freed.

Core Idea
With 'yawma'idh', after-acquired slaves are freed upon entry; without it, only current slaves.

This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq explains a key distinction in conditional emancipation oaths. The inclusion or omission of the word 'yawma'idh' (on that day) determines whether slaves acquired after the oath are included in the emancipation. We will analyze the linguistic reasoning behind this distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two formulations
Recognize the difference between saying 'every slave I own on that day' and 'every slave I own'.
The first includes 'yawma'idh', the second omits it.
2
Understand the role of 'yawma'idh'
Note that 'yawma'idh' refers to the day of entry, not the day of the oath. The tanwin compensates an omitted clause.
3
Apply the ruling to after-acquired slaves
With 'yawma'idh', slaves owned at entry are freed even if acquired after the oath; without it, only those owned at the oath are freed.
4
Consider the case of no ownership at time of oath
If no slaves were owned when the oath was made, the oath is void if 'yawma'idh' is not included.
5
Contrast with statement to a specific slave not owned
If the oath is directed at a specific slave not owned, purchasing and entering does not free the slave because there is no attribution to ownership.

Source Text

(مسكين، فتح) قال: الواو زائدة والأولى إسقاطها وليست استئنافية، وقال العيني في شرح الهداية: إنه تلقى من أفواه الأساتذة أن هذه تسمى واو الاستفتاح (فتح) عتق ما يملك إلخ أي إذا قال: إن دخلت الدار فكل مملوك لي يومئذ حر وليس له مملوك وقت الحلف فاشترى مملوكاً ثم دخل الدار عتق المملوك بدخول الدار؛ لأن معنى قوله: "يومئذ" يوم إذ دخلت الدار، فحذفت الجملة، وعوضها التنوين فاعتبر قيام الملك وقت الدخول، وكذا لو كان في يوم حلف عبد فبقي على ملكه حتى دخل الدار عتق لقيام الملك وقت الدخول. فإن قلت: ينبغي أن لا يعتق من لا يكون في ملكه حلف؛ لأنه ما أضاف العتق إلى الملك ولا إلى سببه، قلت: يوم لم توجد توجد الإضافة صريحاً فقد وجدت دلالة؛ لأن المملوك لا يكون بدون الملك فصار كأنه قال: إن ملكت مملوكا فهو حر وقت دخولي الدار بخلاف قوله لعبد غيره: "إن دخلت الدار فأنت حر فاشتراه ثم دخل الدار لا يعتق؛ لأنه لم توجد الإضافة إلى الملك صريحاً ولا دلالة رمز الحقائق: ۳۳۳/۱] (مستخلص) ولو لم يقل إلخ [ أي في يمينه في الصورة المذكورة (عيني)] أي إذا قال: إن دخلت الدار فكل مملوك لي حر بلا لفظ "يومئذ"، لا يعتق العبد الذي ملكه بعد اليمين؛ لأن قوله: "كل" مملوك لي" للحال، والجزاء حرية المملوك في الحال، إلا أنه لما دخل الشرط على الجزاء تأخر الشرط، فيعتق إذا بقي على ملكه إلى وقت الدخول، ولا يتناول من اشتراه بعده؛ لعدم الإضافة مطلقاً. رمز الحقائق: ۳۳۳/۱] بل يقتصر على المملوك وقت التكلم، فلو لم يكن في ملكه شيء يوم حلف كانت اليمين لغواً. (فتح) لا: أي لا يعتق من ملكه بعد اليمين، بل عتق الذي ملكه وقت اليمين. (ط، عيني) والمملوك لا يتناول الحمل [لأنه عضو من وجه ولفظ المملوك يتناول الأنفس لا الأعضاء. (ف)] لأن لفظ "المملوك" يتناول المطلق، والحمل مملوك تبعاً للأم لا مقصوداً، فلا يدخل تحت المطلق حتى لو قال: "كل مملوك لي حر"، وكان له حمل مملوك بطريق الوصية بأن أوصى له بالحمل فقط، أو قال: "كل" مملوك ذكر لي فهو حر" وله جارية حامل فولدت ذكراً لأقل من ستة أشهر لم يعتق؛ لما ذكرنا، وكذا لا يدخل المكاتب ولا العبد المشترك؛ -
Chapter on vowing by emancipation, i.e., explaining its rulings. And whoever says: 'If I enter the house, then every slave I own on that day is free,' then what he owns afterwards is freed. Meaning: the day when he enters the house. And if he does not say 'on that day,' then no, and the word 'slave' does not include pregnancy. Entering the house even at night. The chapter: vowing by emancipation: 'al-halif' with fathah and sukun on the lam and kasrah on the lam means oath, and with kasrah on the ha and sukun on the lam means covenant. In some copies of the text, 'al-dukhul' is placed instead of 'al-'itq', meaning vowing by emancipation conditional upon entry, but vowing by emancipation is more appropriate because it is clearer. And the meaning is to make emancipation the recompense for the oath by conditioning emancipation on something, so the meaning of 'halif' here is conditional suspension. (Miskin, Fath) He said: the waw is extra and it is better to drop it; it is not isti'nafiyyah. And al-'Ayni said in Sharh al-Hidayah: it is taken from the mouths of teachers that this is called waw al-istiftah (waw of opening). (Fath) 'What he owns afterwards is freed' etc.: meaning if he says: 'If I enter the house, then every slave I own on that day is free' and he has no slave at the time of the oath, then he buys a slave and then enters the house, the slave is freed upon entry, because the meaning of his saying 'yawma'idh' is the day when he enters the house, so the clause is omitted and its tanwin compensates, so ownership at the time of entry is considered. Similarly, if on the day he swore he had a slave and it remained in his ownership until he entered the house, it is freed because ownership exists at the time of entry. If you say: it should not free those who were not in his ownership at the time of the oath, because he did not attribute emancipation to ownership nor to its cause; we say: even if the attribution does not exist explicitly, it exists by indication, because a slave cannot exist without ownership, so it is as if he said: if I own a slave, he is free at the time I enter the house. Contrast with his saying to another's slave: 'If I enter the house, you are free,' then he buys him and enters the house – he is not freed because there is no attribution to ownership explicitly or by indication. (Rumuz al-Haqa'iq: 1/333) (Mustakhlas) 'And if he does not say etc.': meaning in his oath in the mentioned scenario (al-'Ayni). If he says: 'If I enter the house, then every slave I own is free' without the word 'yawma'idh', the slave he owns after the oath is not freed, because his saying 'every slave I own' is for the present, and the recompense is the freeing of the slave at present, except that when the condition enters the recompense, the condition is delayed, so he is freed if he remains in his ownership until the time of entry, and it does not include those he buys afterwards, due to the absolute lack of attribution. (Rumuz al-Haqa'iq: 1/333) Rather, it is limited to the slave at the time of speaking, so if he had no slave on the day of the oath, the oath is void. (Fath) 'No': meaning the one he owns after the oath is not freed; rather, the one he owned at the time of the oath is freed. (T, 'Ayni) 'And the word 'slave' does not include pregnancy': because it is a part from one aspect, and the word 'slave' applies to persons not limbs. (F) Because the word 'slave' applies to absolute, and the fetus is owned as a dependent of the mother, not as an intended object, so it does not fall under the absolute. So even if he says: 'Every slave I own is free' and he has a fetus owned by way of bequest (i.e., someone bequeathed the fetus to him), or he says: 'Every male slave I own is free' and he has a pregnant female slave who gives birth to a male in less than six months, he is not freed for what we mentioned. Similarly, the mukatab (slave under contract) and the jointly owned slave are not included; -
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapter of conditional emancipation oaths. It explains that if a person says 'if I enter the house then every slave I own on that day is free,' the emancipation applies to any slave owned at the moment of entry, even if acquired after the oath, because the phrase 'yawma'idh' (on that day) refers to the day of entry. The tanwin substitutes the omitted clause. Without the word 'yawma'idh', only slaves owned at the time of the oath are included; after-acquired slaves are not freed. The word 'mamluk' (owned slave) does not include a fetus because a fetus is not independently owned; it is owned as a part of the mother. Thus, if someone says 'every slave I own is free' and he has a pregnant slave, the fetus is not freed. Similarly, a mukatab and a jointly-owned slave are not included because they are not fully owned.

Key Terms
الحلف بالعتق (al-halif bil-'itq): A conditional oath where a person makes emancipation the consequence of an action, e.g., 'if I enter the house, this slave is free.'
يومئذ (yawma'idh): A compound word meaning 'on that day'; in this context, it refers to the day of entry, not the day of the oath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man says 'if I enter the house, then every slave I own on that day is free' at a time when he owns no slaves, then later buys a slave and enters the house, what happens?
A) The slave is not freed because he was not owned at the time of the oath.
B) The slave is freed because 'on that day' refers to the day of entry.
C) The oath is invalid because he had no slave at the time.
D) The slave is freed only if he was bought before the oath.

Key Takeaway
The word 'yawma'idh' in a conditional emancipation oath shifts the relevant time of ownership to the moment of entry, thereby including after-acquired slaves.

Scope of 'Mamluk': Exclusion of Pregnancy, Mukatab, and Jointly Owned Slaves
Commentary on the exclusion of certain categories from 'mamluk'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which types of slaves are not included under the term 'mamluk' in conditional emancipation oaths according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The term 'mamluk' does not include a fetus, a mukatab, or a jointly-owned slave.

This commentary continues the discussion on conditional emancipation by clarifying the scope of the word 'mamluk' (owned slave). The Hanafi school specifies that certain categories of slaves are not encompassed by the general term, based on the nature of ownership. We will examine the reasoning for each exclusion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories excluded
List the three categories explicitly excluded: fetus, mukatab, jointly-owned slave.
2
Understand the reasoning for the fetus
The fetus is not considered a separate person; it is owned as a part of the mother, not as an independent entity.
Even if owned separately via bequest, it is still not a 'mamluk' in the intended sense.
3
Understand the reasoning for the mukatab
A mukatab is a slave who has entered a contract to purchase his freedom; his ownership is transitional and not absolute.
4
Understand the reasoning for the jointly-owned slave
A jointly-owned slave is not fully owned by a single master; the term 'my slave' implies exclusive ownership.
5
Apply the rules to scenarios
Given a case with a pregnant slave, a mukatab, or a joint slave, determine whether the oath covers them.
